At this time, the SKWP Cheju branch faced organizational exposure and was in a defensive position. Newly rising elements within the hard-pressed SKWP Cheju branch, exploiting public sentiment turned against the military government, made the decision to wage armed struggle for two purposes: one as a means of protecting and defending the organization, and the other as a "struggle for national salvation" in opposition to the pending separate elections and separate state.

At 2:00 a.m. on April 3, 1948, 350 armed guerrillas attacked twelve police stations and right-wing organizations, launching the armed uprising. These armed guerrillas raised slogans demanding an end to police and Sŏbuk Youth Corps oppression, opposition to separate elections and separate state, and the establishment of a unified government. The American Military Government initially regarded this as a "law and order situation," attempting to suppress the uprising through increased police and Sŏbuk Youth Corps forces. However, when the situation did not subside, Commander of the U.S. Forces in Korea General Hodge and Military Government Administrator General Dean ordered the military police force to deploy suppression operations.

Meanwhile, Major Kim Ik-ryŏl, commander of the 9th Regiment, reached an agreement for peaceful resolution of the crisis through the "April 28 Negotiations" with Kim Tal-sam of the armed guerrillas. However, this peace agreement was broken by the "Orari arson incident" perpetrated by right-wing youth organizations. The American Military Government sought to successfully promote the May 10 elections through the dispatch of Colonel Brown, commander of the 20th Regiment, and Major Shoo, operation officer of the 24th Corps, and the replacement of the 9th Regiment commander. However, in the general elections held on May 10, only two of Cheju's 200 election districts nationwide failed to achieve a majority in voting and were invalidated.

Thereupon, the American Military Government appointed Colonel Brown as supreme commander of the Cheju operational area and launched intense suppression operations, attempting to conduct re-elections on June 23, but failed. On May 20, forty-one military police deserters joined the armed guerrillas, and on June 18, the newly appointed regiment commander Colonel Park Jin-kyŏng was assassinated by his subordinates, shocking the authorities.

After this, the Cheju crisis entered a period of relative calm. The armed guerrillas underwent organizational restructuring, with leaders such as Kim Tal-sam attending the "Hae-ju Conference." The military and police suppression forces, proceeding through the process of government establishment, conducted relatively relaxed suppression operations. However, this calm was short-lived.

With the establishment of the Republic of Korea in South Korea and the founding of another regime in the north, the Cheju situation was now perceived as transcending a mere regional problem and representing a challenge to the legitimacy of the government. The Syngman Rhee government established the Cheju Provincial Military Police Headquarters on October 11 and dispatched mainland military forces to Cheju. However, when the 14th Regiment from Yŏsu, which was intended to be dispatched to Cheju, rebelled against the government, events became swept up in an uncontrollable maelstrom.

**[p. 535]**

Martial law was declared on Cheju Island on November 17. Prior to this, Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an of the 9th Regiment issued a proclamation stating that anyone found traveling more than five kilometers inland from the coastal line in the mid-mountain villages would be regarded as rebel bandits and summarily executed. From this point forward, large-scale hard-line suppression operations were conducted that devastated the mid-mountain villages. In relation to this, an American Military Government intelligence report states: "The 9th Regiment, under the assumption that all residents of villages located in the mid-mountain region clearly provided assistance and convenience to guerrilla forces, adopted a 'program of mass slaughter' against the village residents."

Following the declaration of martial law, the residents of mid-mountain villages suffered extensive damage. Not only in the mid-mountain regions but also relocated residents in coastal villages were killed on the grounds that they had cooperated with the armed guerrillas. As a result, more refugees fled to the mountains to preserve their lives, and when they were captured during the cold winter months hiding on Mount Halla, they were either shot or sent to prisons. Military and police suppression forces even classified families of those missing as "families of evaders" and engaged in "substitute killing," executing parents and siblings instead of the missing person.

At the end of December, the suppression forces were replaced from the 9th Regiment to the 2nd Regiment, but the 2nd Regiment under Commander Hŭm Byŏng-sŏn continued harsh suppression. Residents were summarily executed in groups without judicial proceedings. The "Bukchon Incident," in which the most civilian casualties occurred, was also perpetrated by the 2nd Regiment.

In March 1949, the Cheju District Combat Headquarters was established, and combined suppression and psychological operations were conducted. The newly appointed Commander Yu Chae-hŭng announced an amnesty policy stating that all who descended from Mount Halla would be forgiven. At this time, many residents came down from the mountain. On May 10, 1949, the re-election was successfully held. In June of that year, with the assassination of Yi Tŏk-gu, the armed commander, the armed guerrillas were effectively decimated.

However, when the Korean War broke out, tragedy struck once more. Members of the Podo Yŏnmaeng (National Guidance Alliance), those under investigation, and families of those who had fled to the mountains were arrested en masse and executed. Moreover, members related to the Jeju 4·3 Incident detained in prisons across the country were summarily executed. It is estimated that approximately 3,000 victims resulted from these pre-emptive arrests and prison executions. Bereaved families still have not found most of the bodies.

While there were offensives by remnant armed guerrilla forces, their strength was negligible. On September 21, 1954, the Mt. Halla restricted zone was completely opened. Thus, the Jeju 4·3 Incident, which had been triggered by the March 1 police shooting of 1947 and the April 3 armed uprising of 1948, came to an end after seven years and seven months.

**[p. 536]**

Accordingly, the Jeju 4·3 Incident can be defined as "an incident in which, beginning with the police shooting on March 1, 1947, armed guerrillas of the SKWP Cheju branch launched an armed uprising on April 3, 1948, in opposition to police and Sŏbuk Youth Corps oppression and in opposition to separate elections and separate state, and continuing until the Mt. Halla restricted zone was completely opened on September 21, 1954, numerous civilians were killed in armed clashes between armed guerrillas and suppression forces and in the suppression process by the suppression forces on Cheju Island."

The following matters, which became focal points during this truth investigation, were investigated intensively:

**■ The causes of the uprising were the result of multiple factors.** First, the March 1 shooting incident of 1947 created tension in Cheju society. Subsequently, biased administrative implementation by provincial governors from outside the province, arrest sweeps by police and the Sŏbuk Youth Corps, terrorism, and torture-death incidents created tension. The SKWP Cheju branch, cornered in a defensive position due to organizational exposure, linked this tension to the struggle against the May 10 separate elections, initiating the April 3 armed uprising by attacking police stations.

**■ No evidence has been found of direct instructions from the central SKWP in this process.** However, the fact that armed guerrillas centered on the SKWP Cheju branch killed military and police personnel, election officials, and civilians including police families was clearly a serious wrongdoing. Furthermore, the participation of armed leaders such as Kim Tal-sam in the August 1948 Hae-ju Conference and their support for the establishment of a People's Democratic regime is judged to have accelerated the bloodshed.

**■ The armed guerrillas were an organization under the military affairs division of the SKWP Cheju branch, organized into elite guerrilla units and auxiliary self-defense units, special attack teams, and similar formations.** The personnel mobilized on April 3 are estimated at 350. It is judged that throughout the Jeju 4·3 Incident period, the armed forces never exceeded 500 personnel. Weaponry began with thirty rifles on April 3 and was supplemented through attacks on police stations and the desertion of military police personnel.

**■ It is extremely difficult to determine the exact number of deaths and missing persons—victims—caused by the Jeju 4·3 Incident.** The number of victims reported to this Committee was 14,028. However, this number cannot be regarded as the total number of victims of the entire Jeju 4·3 Incident. Many victims remain unreported or unconfirmed. This investigation, taking into account various sources and population statistics, provisionally estimates the total casualties of the Jeju 4·3 Incident at 25,000 to 30,000 persons. This figure takes into account the 27,719 persons disclosed by Cheju Provincial Governor Kim Yong-ha in April 1950 and the approximately 3,000 casualties resulting from pre-emptive arrests and prison executions following the Korean War. However, it is judged that more precise verification work will be necessary in the future.

**[p. 537]**

**■ Among the victims reported to this Committee, the perpetrator statistics showed suppression forces at 78.1% (10,955 persons), armed guerrillas at 12.6% (1,764 persons), and unknown perpetrators at 9% (1,266 persons).** Excluding the unknown perpetrator category and calculating only the ratio between suppression forces and armed guerrillas, the figures stand at 86.1% and 13.9% respectively. This statistic is consistent with the American military report indicating that over 80% were killed by suppression forces. Particularly noteworthy is that children aged ten or younger (5.8%, 814 persons) and elderly persons aged sixty-one or older (6.1%, 860 persons) comprised 11.9% of all victims, and the large proportion of female victims (21.3%, 2,985 persons) indicates that excessive suppression operations indiscriminately targeted men, women, and children alike.

**■ An estimated 180 or so military personnel were killed in combat during Cheju suppression operations.** Police casualties are identified at 140 deaths. The Sŏbuk Youth Corps members, National Defense Corps members, and other right-wing organization members sacrificed during the Jeju 4·3 Incident are designated as "national merit recipients" subject to government honors. A total of 639 civilians designated as national merit recipients in relation to the Jeju 4·3 Incident are registered with the Veterans Administration.

**■ Sŏbuk Youth Corps members, numbering 500 to 700, entered Cheju prior to the April 3 uprising and had frequent friction with islanders, with their excessive conduct cited as a factor in the uprising's outbreak.** Immediately after the April 3 outbreak, 500 members engaged in suppression activities in Cheju wearing police or military uniforms, and by the end of 1948, approximately 1,000 were so engaged. The torture-death of a director-general of the Cheju Provincial Government Administrative Bureau was perpetrated by the Sŏbuk Youth Corps. Documentary evidence and testimony exist proving that President Syngman Rhee and the United States supported the dispatch of the Sŏbuk Youth Corps to Cheju.

**■ The hard-line suppression operations conducted from November 1948 onward by the 9th Regiment that devastated mid-mountain villages resulted in the most tragic consequences.** The hard-line suppression operations burned more than 95% of mid-mountain villages, and many lives were lost. A total of 39,285 houses were burned in the Jeju 4·3 Incident, with most burned during this period. Ultimately, this hard-line suppression operation resulted in driving approximately 20,000 mid-mountain village residents who had lost their homes into the mountains. During this period, there were also incidents of houses being burned and civilian casualties resulting from armed guerrilla attacks. Representative victim villages were Sehwa, Sŏngŭp, and Namwŏn, with thirty to fifty residents sacrificed from each.

**[p. 538]**

**■ Like the 9th Regiment, the 2nd Regiment that entered Cheju thereafter engaged in summary executions without public judicial proceedings.** The "Bukchon Incident," a representative case of mass civilian executions, was an incident in which approximately 400 residents of a single village, regardless of age or sex, were shot by 2nd Regiment soldiers. According to materials reported to this Committee, forty-five villages experienced casualties exceeding one hundred.

**■ The "April 3 Incident Military Court-Martial," which was reportedly conducted twice—in December 1948 (871 persons) and June 1949 (1,659 persons)—for a total of 2,530 persons, was investigated from multiple angles and found to be no more than a formality. Court records, trial transcripts, and other litigation documents were not discovered; testimony from relevant personnel indicated trials never occurred or sentences were only announced upon arrival at prison; hundreds were processed daily without hearings while 345 death sentences were reportedly handed down in four days—yet this fact was not reported in any domestic press; bodies were clandestinely buried. Given all the circumstances of the period, it is judged that the legally prescribed proper procedures were not followed.**

**■ Regarding the "April 3 Martial Law" declared on November 17, 1948, and lifted on December 31 of the same year, there is dispute between those who argue it was illegal because it took effect without legal basis prior to the enactment of martial law legislation, and those who argue it was legal because Japanese colonial martial law continued to be effective.** Here, setting aside the question of the legal basis for martial law, we wish to point out that the implementation of martial law on Cheju Island deviated from the bounds of law. Frequent summary executions without judicial proceedings occurred under martial law. In particular, military commanders of the period themselves were unfamiliar with martial law, and some platoon commanders of the 2nd Regiment and independent battalions who participated in Cheju operations in 1949 after martial law's lifting testified that they believed martial law remained in effect at that time.

**■ Examining the command structure for mass casualties, primary responsibility must be attributed to the 9th and 2nd Regiment commanders who conducted hard-line operations including mid-mountain village devastation.** During the operational period of these two regiment commanders, from October 1948 to March 1949—a six-month span—over 80% of all casualties occurred. However, ultimate responsibility cannot but fall on President Syngman Rhee. President Syngman Rhee declared martial law and, in a January 1949 state council meeting, stated: "The Americans recognize Korea's importance and express great sympathy, but unless the aftermath of the Cheju and South Jeolla province incidents is completely eradicated and suppressed, their aid will be activated, and local banditry, rebellion, and theft must be suppressed with harsh methods to demonstrate the majesty of law." This investigation revealed that President Rhee gave direct orders for hard-line suppression operations.

**[p. 539]**

**■ In the outbreak and suppression process of the April 3 Incident, neither the American Military Government nor the U.S. Military Advisory Group can escape responsibility.** This incident began under American Military Government rule, and an American colonel directly commanded suppression operations as Cheju district commander. Even after the establishment of the Republic of Korea, the United States, through military agreements between Korea and the U.S., maintained operational control of Korean military forces and provided weapons and reconnaissance aircraft to support Cheju suppression operations. In particular, while rating the 9th Regiment's operations that devastated mid-mountain villages as a "successful operation," the military advisory group commander Brigadier General Roberts requested the Korean government to publicize through presidential statements the activities of Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an.

**■ Damage from guilt-by-association (yŏnzwaaje) was severe.** Regardless of guilt or innocence, bereaved families of victims were placed under surveillance and their social activities restricted solely on the grounds that they had been killed by military and police suppression forces during the April 3 Incident. The scars inflicted by the April 3 Incident on the Cheju community were transmitted to the bereaved families. Cheju residents and bereaved families suffered from "Red Complex" due to guilt-by-association lacking any legal basis. Though guilt-by-association was abolished in 1981, the psychological suffering of bereaved families continues to this day.

The 1948 Genocide Convention, on the prevention and punishment of genocide as a crime, stipulates that genocide is an international crime contrary to the spirit and purpose of the United Nations and must be condemned by the civilized world. The 1949 Geneva Convention specifies that even in wartime, civilian populations are protected from △deliberate killing △torture and inhuman treatment △deliberate harassment or bodily injury △mass destruction and plunder not justifiable for military purposes. Furthermore, it explicitly states that judgments and sentences without trial that do not provide all trial guarantees cannot be recognized.

However, in 1948 on Cheju Island, the basic principles of civilized society demanded by international law were disregarded. In particular, state public authority charged with upholding the law violated the law in killing civilians. The fact that suppression forces killed unarmed civilians without judicial proceedings, particularly the killing of children and elderly persons, constitutes grave human rights violations and serious wrongdoing. In conclusion, Cheju Island became the greatest victim of the Cold War. This very fact served as the factor that suppressed the truth investigation into the April 3 Incident for fifty years.

Despite multifaceted efforts, this report cannot be said to have fully revealed the entire picture of the April 3 Incident. The destruction of relevant documents by police and other major institutions, the refusal to testify by military commanders, and the failure to obtain American classified documents remain sources of regret.

**[p. 540]**

The government must remember this unfortunate event, take it as a lesson, and work to ensure that such tragedy never occurs again. In particular, it is expected that the government will provide comfort to the victims and bereaved families who suffered damages from state public authority and implement appropriate measures for the restoration of honor.

**[p. 541]**

---

[^1]: Republic of Korea, Statistical Summation, No. 5, May 1949, American Embassy Despatch No. 416, July 6, 1949.

[^2]: As of May 1, 1949, the total population of the Republic of Korea was counted as 20,188,641, with Cheju's population at 254,589, representing 1.26% of the total.

**[p. 542]**

*[Blank page in original]*

**[p. 543]**

1. Presidential Statement Regarding the Jeju 4·3 Incident

Respected Cheju Islanders and bereaved families of the Jeju 4·3 Incident, and fellow citizens of the nation,

Fifty-five years ago, on this peaceful Cheju Island, one of the great tragedies of modern Korean history—the 4·3 Incident—occurred. Cheju Islanders suffered tremendous loss of life and destruction of property under the wheels of history brought about by international Cold War and national division.

Before this visit to Cheju, I received a report on the results decided by a committee composed of figures from all walks of life, which was established in accordance with the Special Act on the Clarification of the Truth of the Jeju 4·3 Incident and the Restoration of Honor of the Victims, following more than two years of investigation. The committee has been making recommendations for a government apology regarding the innocent sacrifices that resulted from this incident, the restoration of honor of the victims, and the active promotion of memorial projects.

I believe that now is the time to tie up the historical knot of this unfortunate incident that occurred during the process of government establishment following liberation.

On Cheju Island, beginning with the March 1 incident of 1947, the South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee's armed uprising that occurred on April 3, 1948, and throughout the armed conflicts and suppression process that lasted until September 21, 1954, many people were innocently sacrificed. As President responsible for national governance, I accept the recommendations of the committee, and on behalf of the government, I express my sincere apologies and condolences to the bereaved families and Cheju Islanders for the wrongs committed by past state authority. I bow in respect for the souls of the innocently sacrificed and reverently pray for their peace.

The government will actively support the implementation of the committee's recommendations, including the creation of the 4·3 Peace Park and the prompt restoration of honor of the victims.

Respected fellow citizens,

The work of clarifying the truth of past incidents and restoring the honor of aggrieved victims is not merely for those victims and their bereaved families. While we hold dear the devotion of those who contributed to the founding of the Republic of Korea, it is intended to reveal the truth of history, reflect on the errors of the past, achieve true reconciliation, and promise a brighter future.

Now we must further elevate the precious lessons of the 4·3 Incident and spread the universal human values of "peace and human rights." Through reconciliation and cooperation, we must put an end to all confrontation and division in this land and open the path toward peace on the Korean Peninsula, and further, toward peace in Northeast Asia and the world.

Cheju Islanders have rebuilt this beautiful island of peace called Cheju by overcoming devastation with their bare hands. I express my sincere respect to the Cheju people.

Cheju Island will now stand tall as a symbol of human rights and an island of peace. Together with all citizens of the nation, I will help make this so.

Thank you.

October 31, 2003
President Noh Mu-hyŏn

**[p. 544]**

2. Chronology of the Jeju 4·3 Incident

1947

3.1 — The Jeju Civil Committee held the 28th anniversary March 1 Independence Movement commemoration ceremony. Gunfire by riot police resulted in 6 residents killed and 8 with serious injuries in front of Kwandŏk Pavilion and the Provincial Hospital, resulting in the "March 1 Incident."

3.5 — The "March 1 Incident Countermeasures Struggle Committee" of the South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee was formed.

3.7 — The South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee issued directives to each county/township committee regarding "struggle concerning countermeasures to the March 1 Incident."

3.8 — A joint investigative team from the U.S. military government and U.S. Army Military Government in Korea (Chief: Colonel Caster) arrived on the island to investigate the March 1 Incident.

3.10 — Beginning with the Cheju Provincial Government, all government and civic organs and organizations went on strike to protest the March 1 Incident. By the 13th, 166 institutions and organizations, representing 95% of all workplaces on Cheju Island, participated in the strike.

3.12 — Deputy Chief of Police Choi Kyŏng-jin, in mentioning the Cheju strike situation, stated: "Originally, 90% of Cheju Island residents have leftist tendencies."

3.14 — Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok arrived on the island to investigate the circumstances of the Cheju strike. He issued a proclamation. Young men from Udo destroyed and burned the signboard of the Udo police substation. Cheju Island Governor Park Kyŏng-hun submitted his resignation to Military Government Chief Staud.

3.15 — 222 reinforcement police, including 122 from South Chŏlla Province and 100 from North Chŏlla Province, arrived on Cheju Island. Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok issued an order to arrest those who had incited the strikes.

Mid-March — U.S. CIC established an office on Cheju.

3.16 — A Special Investigation Section (Chief: Lee Ho) was established within the Cheju Police Surveillance and Inspection Bureau, centered on police officers from the mainland. Supervisory personnel from striking workplaces were brought in for interrogation.

3.17 — Reinforcement police from Chungchŏng at Chungmun Substation fired on a crowd demanding the release of detainees, injuring 8 residents.

3.18 — 99 police from Kyŏnggi Province arrived on Cheju Island. Reinforcement police increased to a total of 421. Police Chief Kang In-su of the Cheju Surveillance and Inspection Bureau announced: "About 200 people have been detained in connection with the March 1 Incident."

3.20 — Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok, in a statement regarding the investigation of the March 1 Incident, announced: "The gunfire at the First District Police Station is recognized as legitimate self-defense, and the gunfire in front of the Provincial Hospital is recognized as an act of inadvertence." The U.S. military intelligence team reported: "Both leftists and rightists participated in Cheju's general strike, and 70% of Cheju Islanders are sympathizers of leftist organizations."

3.22 — The South Korean Labor Party conducted a nationwide "March 22 General Strike" lasting 24 hours.

3.24 — Sin U-gyun, the former head of the Cheju Surveillance and Inspection Bureau involved in the misconduct case, was dismissed by the Personnel Committee of the Police Bureau.

**[p. 545]**

3.26 — In response to the arrest of teachers, parents of students at Cheju Northern School demanded the release of detained teachers.

3.28 — The Police Bureau announced: "A total of 2,176 strike agitators were arrested nationwide, 230 in Cheju."

3.31 — Some ten senior officials of the Cheju Provincial Government, including Director of Industry Lim Kwan-ho, were detained.

4.1 — Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok announced that 66 police officers from Cheju who participated in the strike incident had been dismissed through disciplinary action.

4.2 — Colonel Beros was appointed as military government chief of Cheju Island.

4.10 — Yi Hae-jin, from North Chŏlla Province, was appointed Cheju Island governor. The Cheju Police Surveillance and Inspection Bureau announced that there were 500 detention cases from the strike, of which 260 had been referred to military courts.

4.28 — 245 railway police were assigned to the Cheju Police as replacement reinforcements. The Cheju Police force increased to 500 personnel. A recruitment advertisement in the Cheju Sinbo, signed by the 9th Regiment commander Major Chang Chang-kuk, stated: "The Defense Force is neither leftist nor rightist."

5.6 — The Cheju Prosecutor's Office announced: "328 defendants in the March 1 Incident were transferred from the Police Surveillance Bureau."

5.7 — Some 400 reinforcement police withdrew from Cheju.

5.21 — The second Korea-Soviet Joint Commission was reconvened. The U.S. brought the Korean Peninsula issue to the United Nations.

5.23 — The trial of 328 people referred in connection with the March 1 Incident was completed. Sentences: 52 persons imprisoned, 52 suspended, 56 fined, and the remaining 168 cases were granted prosecutorial discretion or not prosecuted.

5.24 — Police Chief Kang Dong-hyo of the First District Station was dismissed over a bribery case.

5.26 — Two police officers, including the Hallim Substation commander, were arrested in connection with torture of suspects.

6.1 — Police detained 20 middle school students in Cheju town on suspicion of distributing leaflets.

6.2 — Third-year students at Cheju Girls' Middle School went on strike demanding opposition to fascist education.

6.6 — In Chongdal-ri, Kujwa-myŏn, three police officers on crowd control duty were beaten by local youths in the incident known as the "June 6 Incident."

6.16 — Cheju Police announced: "Persons being sought in connection with the Chongdal-ri Incident number 71."

6.18 — Ten students from the Teacher Training Institute and Chojŏn Middle School, prosecuted for distributing leaflets, were sentenced.

6.20 — Young people from various villages were brought to trial for suspicion of distributing leaflets.

6.22 — The Cheju Sinbo reported that "condolence money for bereaved families of March 1 victims" totaled 317,118 wŏn.

July — The Cheju Civil Committee (Chairman Hyŏn Kyŏng-ho) officially registered as an organization on Cheju Island and was refounded.

7.3 — When a student punished with expulsion for receiving a suspended sentence in a leaflet-distribution case, third-year students at Cheju Agricultural School objected and staged a sit-in protest.

7.14 — Cheju Police Surveillance and Inspection Bureau Chief Kim Yŏng-bae, after attending a chief's conference, stated: "In Cheju alone, I am determined to work on a cooperation movement to ensure that leftists and rightists join hands."

7.18 — Former Cheju Island Governor Park Kyŏng-hun was nominated as chairman of the Cheju Civil Committee.

7.19 — Yŏ Un-hyŏng, leader of the Labor Peasant Party, was assassinated.

7.28 — Cheju Island Military Government Chief Colonel Beros stated: "Whether members of leftist or rightist political parties, they can be employed as government officials. This is the principle of democracy."

End of July — At Myŏngwol-ri, Hallim-myŏn, farmers refusing to meet grain collection quotas clashed with rightist youth group members.

8.7 — Anti-American leaflets stating "Drive out U.S. troops" circulated in Cheju. The Cheju CIC reported: "The extreme-right Cheju Island governor is unpopular among leftists. Several leaflets demanding his assassination have been distributed."

8.8 — In Tonggwang-ri, Andŏk-myŏn, government officials visiting the village to encourage barley sales were beaten by local youths.

8.12 — The U.S. military government initiated large-scale arrests of leftist forces in connection with the "August 15 Rebellion Plot Incident." A total of 13,769 people were detained nationwide.

8.13 — In Pukch'on-ri, Chojŏn-myŏn, police fired while pursuing a boy posting leaflets, wounding 3 residents.

8.14 — Cheju Police arrested some twenty people, including Cheju Civil Committee Chairman Park Kyŏng-hun, former Cheju Island governor, provincial government officials, and social leaders, in connection with the "August 15 Rebellion Plot."

8.17 — Those detained in connection with the "August 15 Rebellion Plot," including Cheju Civil Committee Chairman Park Kyŏng-hun, were released.

8.19 — Leaflets opposing grain collection circulated throughout Cheju Island.

8.28 — Governor Yŏ Hae-jin began personnel restructuring, initiating with the voluntary resignation of Learning Superintendent Yi Kwan-sŏk and three other bureau-chief-level officials on grounds of ideological issues.

8.31 — Grain collection rate: nationwide 67.6%, Cheju Island only 13.7%.

9.7 — Cheju Island Food Bureau Chief Park Tae-hun was terrorized at his home by unidentified youths. Investigation revealed it was done by Northwest Youth Association members.

9.8 — Former chairman of Cheju Civil Committee Hyŏn Kyŏng-ho: A residence belonging to the principal of Cheju Middle School was attacked by a youth impersonating a Surveillance Bureau official. Investigation by the Cheju CIC revealed it was done by Northwest Youth Association members.

9.17 — The second Korea-Soviet Joint Commission was dissolved. The United States submitted the Korean Peninsula issue to the United Nations.

9.21 — Twenty-two rightist youth organizations unified and the Great Eastern Youth Organization was established.

9.27 — The Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau's Investigation Section detained 36 people, including staff from the Essential Goods Trading Company, teachers at Cheju Agricultural School and Cheju Middle School, alleging they had discovered seditious materials.

10.6 — Cheju District Court handed down a suspended sentence to former Cheju Civil Committee Chairman An Sae-hun, who had led the March 1 gathering.

10.7 — In Haengwŏn-ri, Kujwa-myŏn, members of the Youth Association clashed with local youths. Five Youth Association members and eleven local youths were arrested.

10.18 — The Police Support Association (Chairman Hong Sun-yong) was formed.

10.19 — The Cheju CIC reported: "Members of the Great Eastern Youth Organization, who were conducting membership expansion activities, engaged in terrorist activities in villages at the eastern end of Cheju Island. Investigation by CIC is underway."

10.21 — The Great Eastern Youth Organization, Cheju branch, which had been divided into Conservative and Progressive factions, agreed to unify.

10.24 — The Cheju CIC reported to its superiors: "The recent unification of the Great Eastern Youth Organization was achieved 'through our efforts.'"

11.2 — The Northwest Youth Association, Cheju Provincial Headquarters (Chair: Chang Tong-ch'un) was established.

11.3 — Lieutenant General Dean took office as the third head of the U.S. Military Government. Police Chief Kim Yŏng-bae of the Cheju Surveillance and Inspection Bureau issued a warning statement, noting widespread complaints about illegal donation demands by private organizations.

11.5 — Travel restriction hours were changed from 10 p.m. to 5 a.m.

11.12 — Lieutenant Colonel Nelson, special inspector of the U.S. military government, initiated a special investigation into Cheju Island Governor Yŏ Hae-jin. This investigation continued until February 28, 1948.

11.14 — The UN General Assembly passed the U.S. proposal for "general elections based on population ratio" on the Korean Peninsula.

11.18 — The Cheju CIC reported: "The leader of the Northwest Youth Association received a warning regarding widespread terrorist activities for fundraising on Cheju Island and apologized to the CIC."

11.21 — Legal Officer Stevenson of the Cheju Military Government and CIC Representative Merit submitted an opinion to the special investigation team stating: "Governor Yŏ Hae-jin permits no gatherings except rightist meetings."

11.25 — The Cheju CIC reported to its superiors that the Northwest Youth Association's Cheju branch director had been saying "Cheju Island is Korea's little Moscow."

11.26 — Military Government Chief Dean visited Cheju Island for inspection. He left on the 28th.

12.3 — Colonel Mansfield was appointed as Cheju Island's new military government chief, replacing Colonel Beros.

12.7 — The Cheju CIC reported to superiors: "If government authorities do not take measures regarding the Cheju police, bloodshed could occur."

12.26 — Cheju Island's achievement rate in purchasing old grain was 11%, the lowest in the nation (84.5%).

1948

1.8 — The UN Korean Temporary Commission arrived in Seoul.

Mid-January — The organizational liaison representative of the South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee was arrested by police. With the person's conversion, the organizational structure of the South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee was exposed.

1.22 — The Cheju CIC reported: "Cheju police raided an illegal meeting place of the South Korean Labor Party's Chojŏn Branch at Sinch'on-ri, arrested 106 people, and seized inflammatory documents."

1.26 — In addition to the 106 arrested on January 22, another 115 were arrested. The Cheju CIC reported: "Of the 221 arrested, 63 were released, and they had been South Korean Labor Party members."

1.30 — Police Chief Kim Yŏng-bae of the Cheju Surveillance and Inspection Bureau, regarding the "January 22 arrest incident," announced: "Police are not suppressing those who joined the South Korean Labor Party, but rather striking down their illegal activities."

2.1 — Deputy Regiment Commander Major Kim Ik-ryŏl was appointed to replace Regiment Commander Lieutenant Colonel Yi Ch'i-ŏp of the 9th Regiment.

2.7 — Martial alert declared nationwide. Leftist forces conducted the "February 7 Struggle," a nationwide general strike opposing the single-nation elections in South Korea.

2.8 — At Hamdŏk-ri, Chojŏn-myŏn, youths set up a barricade and clashed with a provincial government vehicle driver who was attempting to remove walls. Police who responded urgently arrested 12 youths.

2.9 — Youths at Sagye-ri, Andŏk-myŏn, beat two police officers who were drinking in the village. The Chŏji Substation was attacked by youths.

2.10 — Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok announced: "In connection with the 'February 7 Rebellion,' 39 people nationwide have died and 8,479 have been arrested." Police at Kosan Substation fired on demonstrators, seriously wounding 1 resident.

2.11 — Cheju police reported that in the aftermath of the "February 7 Incident," 1 arson, 9 terrorism incidents, and 19 protest incidents occurred in Cheju. In three days, 290 people were arrested.

2.26 — The UN Temporary Assembly adopted the U.S. proposal: "Single elections will be held in regions accessible to the UN Korean Commission."

End of February — At a meeting of the South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee leadership in Sinch'on-ri, following a debate between hard and soft-liners, the armed struggle policy was decided by a vote of 12 to 7.

3.6 — Kim Yong-ch'ŏl, a Chojŏn Middle School student, died from torture during interrogation at Chojŏn Substation.

3.10 — Chojŏn Middle School students and residents gathered at the substation to protest the torture death. In Sŏngsan-myŏn, 66 young men issued a statement announcing their withdrawal from the South Korean Labor Party and enrollment in the Great Eastern Youth Organization. Subsequently, announcements of withdrawal from the South Korean Labor Party continued.

3.11 — Special Inspector Lieutenant Colonel Nelson of the U.S. military government, in his special investigation report regarding Cheju Island Governor Yŏ Hae-jin, recommended to Military Government Chief Dean the removal of Governor Yŏ, investigation of Cheju police administration, and investigation of overcrowded detention areas.

3.14 — In Moseulpo Substation, the torture death of Yang Ŭn-ha, a young man from Yŏngnak-ri, Taejŏng-myŏn, occurred.

3.15 — At a meeting of the South Korean Labor Party's upper Cheju leadership, attended by an organizational representative from the South Chŏlla Province Party, the armed struggle was finally decided for two reasons: First, as a means of protecting and defending the organization; second, as a "national salvation struggle" against single-nation elections and divided government.

3.20 — A clash occurred at a new star hill in Aewŏl-myŏn between trainees of the self-defense unit and police from Aewŏl Substation, members of the Northwest Youth Association, and members of the Youth Organization.

3.28 — Syngman Rhee expressed his willingness to place Cheju Island at the disposal of the U.S. as a military base to U.S. Secretary of the Army Draper, who was visiting Korea. The South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee held a meeting and decided to begin the armed struggle on April 3.

**[p. 546]**

## 2. Chronology of the Jeju 4.3 Incident

**[March 26]** Jeju North School parents demand release of arrested teachers in response to successive teacher arrests

**[March 28]** Ministry of Police announces "2,176 strike agitators arrested nationwide, with 230 in Jeju"

**[March 31]** About ten senior officials from Jeju Provincial Government Office, including Provincial Industrial Bureau Director Im Kwan-ho, arrested

**[April 1]** Police Chief Cho Byong-ok announces disciplinary dismissal of 66 Jeju police officers who participated in the strike incident

**[April 2]** Colonel Verros appointed Military Governor of Jeju Province

**[April 10]** You Hae-jin, from North Cholla Province, appointed Jeju Province Governor

Jeju Police Surveillance Office announces 500 arrested in the strike; 260 referred to military court

**[April 28]** 245 railroad police transferred to Jeju police as replacement forces for relief police; Jeju police strength increased to 500

Colonel Chang Chang-guk, Commander of the 9th Regiment, publishes recruitment advertisement for National Defense Forces in Jeju Daily News stating "The National Defense Forces are neither left nor right"

**[May 6]** Jeju Prosecutors' Office announces "328 defendants from the March 1 incident transferred from the Police Surveillance Office"

**[May 7]** About 400 relief police withdraw from Jeju

**[May 21]** US-Soviet Joint Commission reconvenes

Colonel Lee Chi-op takes office as successor to 9th Regiment Commander Chang Chang-guk

**[May 23]** Trials completed for 328 persons referred to court in the March 1 incident; 52 sentenced to imprisonment, 52 suspended sentences, 56 fined; remaining 168 receive prosecutorial discretion or dismissal

**[May 24]** First District Police Station Chief Kang Dong-hyo dismissed for bribery

**[May 26]** Two police officers, including Hallim Police Substation Chief, arrested for torture of suspects

**[June 1]** Police arrest 20 middle school students from Jeju town on suspicion of distributing leaflets

**[June 2]** Third-year students at Jeju Girls Middle School stage sympathy strike demanding cessation of fascist education and other requirements

**[June 6]** The so-called "June 6 Incident" occurs: three police officers monitoring a Democratic Youth Assembly in Jongdal-ri, Gujwa-myeon, are assaulted by village youth

**[June 16]** Jeju police announce "Wanted persons in the Jongdal-ri incident number 71"

**[June 18]** Ten students from Normal School and Chocheon Middle School, prosecuted for posting leaflets, receive sentences

**[June 20]** Youth from various villages referred to trial on suspicion of distributing leaflets

**[June 22]** Jeju Daily News reports that "condolence funds for bereaved families of March 1 incident victims" total 317,118 won

**[July]** Jeju Provincial Democratic Front (Chairman Hyeon Kyong-ho) registers as organization and reorganizes in Jeju Province

**[July 3]** After a student receiving a suspended sentence for the leaflet incident is expelled, third-year students at Jeju Agricultural School stage protest demonstration

**[July 14]** Jeju Police Surveillance Office Chief Kim Young-bae states at Surveillance Chiefs Conference that "Jeju Province should make efforts in cooperative movement where left and right join hands"

**[p. 547]**

**[July 18]** Former Jeju Province Governor Park Kyong-hun elected Chairman of Jeju Province Democratic Front

**[July 19]** Leader of the Korean Workers' Party Yeo Un-hyong assassinated

**[July 28]** Military Governor Colonel Verros states "Regardless of whether left or right political parties and their members, they can take positions as government or public employees. This is the principle of democracy"

**[Late July]** Collision occurs between farmers refusing grain collection and right-wing youth group members in Myongwol-ri, Hallim-myeon

**[August 7]** Anti-American leaflets reading "Expel American troops" circulate in Jeju

Jeju CIC reports "The extreme right-wing Jeju Province Governor is unpopular among leftists. Several leaflets demanding his assassination have been distributed"

**[August 8]** Government officials visiting Andok-myeon Donggwang-ri to encourage barley purchase are assaulted by village youth

**[August 12]** US Military Government begins large-scale arrest operation against leftist forces in connection with the "August 15 Rebellion Plot Incident"; 13,769 arrested nationwide

**[August 13]** In pursuit of a boy posting leaflets in Sacheon-ri, Chocheon-myeon, police fire, wounding three residents

**[August 14]** Jeju police arrest about twenty people including former Jeju Province Governor and Jeju Democratic Front Chairman Park Kyong-hun, provincial government officials, and community leaders in connection with the "August 15 Rebellion Plot"

**[August 17]** Jeju Democratic Front Chairman Park Kyong-hun and others arrested in connection with the "August 15 Rebellion Plot" are released

**[August 19]** Leaflets opposing grain collection distributed throughout Jeju Province

**[August 28]** Governor You Hae-jin initiates personnel reorganization beginning with recommending dismissal of four provincial bureau chiefs including Education Bureau Director Lee Kwan-sok on grounds of ideological problems

**[August 31]** Grain collection rate for entire nation 67.6%; Jeju Province only 13.7%

**[September 7]** Jeju Province Food Administration Director Park Tae-hun terrorized at his home by unidentified youth; revealed to be work of Western Youth Corps members

**[September 8]** Former Jeju Province Democratic Front Chairman Hyeon Kyong-ho's house at Jeju Middle School Principal's residence attacked by youth impersonating Surveillance Office employee; Jeju CIC investigation reveals work of Western Youth Corps members

**[September 17]** Second US-Soviet Joint Commission deadlocked. United States brings Korea question to UN

**[September 21]** Twenty-two right-wing youth organizations merge; Great Oriental Youth Corps founded

**[September 27]** Jeju Police Surveillance Office Investigation Division arrests 36 people including staff of Consumer Goods Cooperative and teachers from Jeju Agricultural School and Jeju Middle School on grounds of discovering subversive documents

**[October 6]** Jeju District Court sentences former Jeju Province Democratic Front Chairman An Sae-hun, who led the March 1 assembly, to suspended sentence

**[October 7]** Collision between Great Oriental Corps members and local youth in Haeongwon-ri, Gujwa-myeon; five Great Oriental Corps members and eleven local youth arrested

**[October 18]** Police Support Association (President Hong Sun-yong) established

**[October 19]** Jeju CIC reports "Great Oriental Youth Corps members conducting party expansion campaign engaged in terrorist acts in an eastern village of Jeju Province; investigation underway at CIC"

**[p. 548]**

**[October 21]** Great Oriental Youth Corps Jeju Provincial Unit, divided into Independence and Patriotic groups, agree to integration

**[October 24]** Jeju CIC reports to superiors "Recent integration of the Great Oriental Youth Corps was accomplished through 'our efforts'"

**[November 2]** Northwestern Youth Corps Jeju Province Division (Chairman Chang Dong-chun) established

**[November 3]** Colonel Dean takes office as 3rd Chief of US Military Government in Korea

Police Surveillance Office Chief Kim Young-bae issues warning regarding grievances over illegal fundraising demands by private organizations

**[November 5]** Curfew time changed from 10 PM to 5 AM

**[November 12]** US Military Government Special Inspector Colonel Nelson begins special investigation of Jeju Province Governor You Hae-jin. Investigation continues through February 28, 1948

**[November 14]** UN General Assembly passes US proposal for elections on Korea by proportional representation

**[November 18]** Jeju CIC reports "Northwestern Youth Corps leaders warned about widespread terrorist acts to raise funds in Jeju Province; made apology to CIC"

**[November 21]** Jeju Military Government Law Officer Stephenson and Jeju CIC representative Merritt submit opinion to special investigation team stating "Governor You Hae-jin permits no assemblies except right-wing ones"

**[November 25]** Jeju CIC reports to superiors that Northwestern Youth Corps Jeju Province Commander has referred to "Jeju Province as a small Moscow of Korea"

**[November 26]** Military Government Chief Dean visits Jeju Province for inspection; departs on 28th

**[December 3]** Colonel Mansfield appointed Jeju Province Military Governor, succeeding Colonel Verros

**[December 7]** Jeju CIC reports to superiors "If police authorities take no action regarding Jeju Province police, bloodshed may occur"

**[December 26]** Jeju Province fall grain purchase performance 11%; worst in nation compared to 84.5% nationwide

**1948**

**[January 8]** UN Temporary Commission on Korea arrives in Seoul

**[Mid-January]** Liaison officer of Organization Department of South Korean Labor Party Jeju Province Committee arrested by police; arrests lead to exposure of organizational structure of South Korean Labor Party Jeju Province

**[January 22]** Jeju CIC reports "Jeju police raided illegal South Korean Labor Party Chocheon Branch meeting in Sinchon-ri; arrested 106 and confiscated documents including insurrection directives"

**[p. 549]**

**[January 26]** In addition to 106 arrested on January 22, 115 more arrested. Jeju CIC reports "Of 221 detained, 63 released; they were South Korean Labor Party members"

**[January 30]** Police Surveillance Office Chief Kim Young-bae announces regarding the January 22 arrest incident: "Police do not suppress those who joined the South Korean Labor Party, but strike with force against their illegal acts"

**[February 1]** Lieutenant Colonel Kim Ik-ryol appointed as successor to 9th Regiment Commander Lieutenant Colonel Lee Chi-op; Major Kim assumes duties as deputy regiment commander

**[February 7]** National alert throughout country

Left-wing forces conduct "February 7 Struggle" engaging entire nation in general strike opposing separate South Korean elections

**[February 8]** In Hamdok-ri, Chocheon-myeon, youth block road and collide with Provincial Government Office vehicle driver removing wall barrier; police respond urgently, arresting 12 youths

**[February 9]** Youth in Sagye-ri, Andok-myeon gang-assault two police officers drinking in village

Joji Police Substation attacked by youth

**[February 10]** Police Chief Cho Byong-ok announces "39 killed and 8,479 arrested from the February 7 insurrection nationwide"

Police at Gosan Police Substation fire on assembled crowd; one resident severely wounded

**[February 11]** Jeju police announce regarding aftermath of February 7 incident: "One arson, nine terrorist acts, nineteen demonstrations occurred in Jeju; 290 arrested over three days"

**[February 26]** UN Interim Assembly adopts US proposal for separate elections "in areas accessible to the UN Commission on Korea"

**[Late February]** South Korean Labor Party Jeju Province Committee officials debate "strong faction" versus "moderate faction" at Sinchon Conference; armed struggle direction decided 12-7

**[March 6]** Chocheon Middle School student Kim Yong-chol dies under torture during interrogation at Chocheon Police Substation

**[March 10]** Chocheon Middle School students and residents gather at police substation to protest torture death

Sixty-six youth in Sungsan-myeon announce statement withdrawing from South Korean Labor Party and joining Great Oriental Youth Corps; followed by additional withdrawal statements

**[March 11]** US Military Government Special Inspector Colonel Nelson recommends to Military Government Chief Dean dismissal of Governor You Hae-jin, investigation of Jeju Province police administration, investigation of overcrowded police detention cells

**[March 14]** Torture death incident occurs: youth Yang Un-ha from Youngnak-ri, Daejong-myeon dies under torture at Mosulpo Police Substation

**[March 15]** South Korean Labor Party Jeju Province Leadership reaches final decision on armed struggle at meeting with North Cholla Province Organizer as means of: first, protecting and defending existing organization; second, conducting "national salvation struggle" opposing separate elections and separate government

**[March 20]** Collision occurs between self-defense corps members in training at Saebbyol Peak, Aewol-myeon and police, Western Youth Corps, and Great Oriental Youth Corps members at Aewol Police Substation

**[March 28]** Syngman Rhee expresses willingness to provide Jeju Province as US military base to visiting US Army Secretary Assistant Secretary Draper

South Korean Labor Party Jeju Province Committee holds meeting deciding April 3 as start date of armed struggle

**[p. 550]**

3.29 — At Kumnung-ri, Hallim-myŏn, young man Park Haeng-gu, who had been criticizing the U.S. military government, was captured by police and the Northwest Youth Association and summarily executed.

3.30 — Electoral registration work for the May 10 general elections began throughout the country.

4.1 — The National Assembly Electoral Commission announced the number of National Assembly members by province. Cheju Island was allocated 3 out of 200 total members.

4.3 — The armed uprising broke out on Cheju Island. Some 350 armed personnel of the South Korean Labor Party's Cheju Provincial Committee, at 2 a.m., attacked 12 police substations throughout the island and assaulted residences of rightist leaders. 4 police, 8 civilians, and 2 armed guerrillas were killed.

4.5 — The U.S. military government hastily sent about 100 police officers from South Chŏlla Province as reinforcements and established the Cheju Emergency Security Command (Commander: Kim Chŏng-ho, Director of the Police Bureau's Public Safety Division) within the Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau. The U.S. military government proclaimed a proclamation isolating Cheju Island's sea traffic and implemented a naval blockade with U.S. naval vessels.

4.8 — The U.S. decided provisionally to withdraw its forces from Korea by the end of December 1948. Cheju Emergency Security Commander Kim Chŏng-ho issued a proclamation stating that a mopping-up operation against the armed guerrillas would be launched.

4.10 — One hundred personnel from the National Police Officer Training School were dispatched to Cheju.

4.13 — The 9th Regiment dispatched a special unit to Cheju town to maintain security and order in the Northern Cheju District.

4.14 — Final electoral registration results: In Cheju Island, 82,812 out of 127,752 registered, achieving 64.9% (national average 91.7%), the lowest in the nation. Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok announced a proclamation of persuasion.

4.16 — By order of Military Government Chief Dean, propaganda units were established throughout South Korea. Police Public Information Director Kim Tae-bong was dispatched to Cheju to conduct persuasion activities on the special order of Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok.

4.17 — By order of Military Government Chief Dean via Colonel Mansfield, the 9th Regiment was ordered to cooperate with police and participate in suppression operations.

4.18 — Military Government Chief Dean ordered Colonel Mansfield to exercise operational control over the defense force stationed in Cheju and to negotiate with armed guerrilla leaders. The armed guerrillas attacked election administration offices and stole related documents. Governor Yŏ Hae-jin and 32 others formed the State-of-Nation Countermeasures Committee.

4.19 — Armed guerrillas attacked and set fire to the voting place at Sinch'on-ri, Chojŏn-myŏn.

4.20 — The U.S. military government dispatched Captain Druse, a U.S. advisor, and one company of the 5th Regiment from Busan to Cheju Island.

4.22 — The Cheju Emergency Security Command changed the nighttime travel ban from 8 p.m. to 5 a.m. the following morning. Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryŏl of the 9th Regiment dropped leaflets by airplane requesting peace negotiations with the armed guerrillas.

4.24 — The Washington Post published the first report on the Cheju incident under the headline "Korea Island Rebellion: 46 Dead."

4.27 — In Cheju, U.S. 20th Regiment Commander Colonel Brown, 24th Army Operations Staff Chief Major Shu, and Military Government Chief Colonel Mansfield held a meeting to discuss countermeasures. A search operation was conducted mobilizing the Defense Force 5th Regiment and U.S. 20th Regiment reconnaissance.

4.28 — Ninth Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryŏl and armed guerrilla leader Kim Dal-sam engaged in peace negotiations. They agreed to cease combat within 72 hours.

4.29 — Military Government Chief Dean visited Cheju Island in secrecy. Major Shu submitted a report to the effect that the current troop strength in Cheju Island was sufficient to stabilize the situation. Cheju Emergency Security Commander Kim Chŏng-ho stated: "We are conducting forceful operations prohibiting traffic throughout the island after 8 p.m., and violators will be shot."

5.1 — The so-called "Orari Arson Incident" occurred, breaking the peace negotiations. Armed guerrillas killed the chairman of the elections management committee at Dopae-ri, Cheju town.

5.3 — U.S. military leaders ordered the Defense Force Command to "conduct a total assault against the armed guerrillas and resolve the Cheju Incident within a short time." The New York Times reported that the armed guerrillas on Cheju Island presented five conditions for surrender, including "confiscation of police weapons, punishment of police and Northwest Youth Association members, and cancellation of the May 10 election."

5.5 — In the meeting room of the U.S. military government in Cheju town, Military Government Chief Dean, Civil Minister An Chae-hong, Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok, Defense Force Commander Song Ho-sŏng, Colonel Mansfield, Governor Yŏ Hae-jin, 9th Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryŏl, and Chief of Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau Ch'oe Ch'ŏn held the so-called "May 5 Top-Level Conference." Armed guerrillas killed the elections management committee chairman at Hwabok-ri and the district chief at Naedo-ri.

5.6 — The U.S. military government dismissed Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryŏl of the 9th Regiment and appointed Colonel Park Chin-kyŏng as the new 9th Regiment commander.

5.10 — The May 10 election was held. Cheju Island recorded the lowest voting rate of 62.8%. The Kap and Ul election districts in Northern Cheju County were nullified due to insufficient turnout. Armed guerrillas attacked the Sangyae-ri District 2 at Chungmun-myŏn, kidnapped and killed the Youth Association district chief couple and the National Association's Sangyae-ri representative.

5.11 — Armed guerrillas at Todu-ri, Cheju town, kidnapped and successively killed from the 11th through the 19th of May, the village elections management committee chairman, Great Eastern Youth Organization leaders, and their family members.

5.12 — The U.S. military government hastily dispatched the destroyer USS Craig to Cheju Island to continue the coastal blockade.

5.15 — The 11th Regiment moved from Suwŏn to Cheju (with the 9th Regiment Commander Colonel Park Chin-kyŏng assuming the position of 11th Regiment Commander). The existing 9th Regiment was consolidated into the 11th Regiment.

5.18 — The National Assembly Elections Commission recommended to Military Government Chief Dean that elections in the Kab and Ŭl districts of Northern Cheju County be nullified.

5.19 — A special investigation team led by Police Senior Inspector Ch'oe Nan-su and 450 officers in total, including 350 railway police and 100 police from the 6th and 8th police districts, were dispatched to Cheju on the order of the Police Bureau.

5.20 — The U.S. military government dispatched Colonel Brown, commander of the 20th Regiment stationed in Kwangju under the U.S. 6th Division, as the Cheju District U.S. military commander. 41 defense force personnel deserted from the Moseulpo base.

5.21 — The U.S. military government announced that O Yong-kuk had been elected as a National Assembly member in Southern Cheju County.

5.22 — Of the 41 deserting defense force personnel, 20 were captured near Taejŏng.

5.25 — The South Korean Labor Party's newspaper, Labor and Peasants, published its first report on the Cheju situation.

5.26 — Military Government Chief Dean announced the nullification of the elections in the Kab and Ŭl election districts of Northern Cheju County and declared that reelections would be held on June 23.

5.28 — Cheju Island Governor Yŏ Hae-jin was removed and replaced by Im Kwan-ho, a Cheju native. Police Chief Cho Byŏng-ok visited Cheju Island to inspect the security situation.

5.31 — The Constitutional Assembly convened. Syngman Rhee was elected National Assembly speaker.

Late May — General Roberts, advisor to the Liaison Bureau, inspected Cheju Island.

6.1 — 11th Regiment Commander Park Chin-kyŏng was promoted to colonel.

6.2 — U.S. Military Commander Brown of the forces stationed in Cheju stated: "We are conducting operations to sweep from the western to the eastern end of Cheju Island."

6.10 — Military Government Chief Dean issued Administrative Order No. 22, postponing indefinitely the reelections in the Kab and Ŭl districts of Northern Cheju that were scheduled for June 23.

6.11 — Chief of Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau Ch'oe Ch'ŏn was suspended from office due to insufficient supervision.

6.17 — Kim Bong-ho, a Cheju native, was appointed as Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau Chief.

6.18 — Regiment Commander Park Chin-kyŏng of the 11th Regiment was killed by a subordinate at his quarters. Military Government Chief Dean and General Roberts came to Cheju to investigate the situation and collected the remains before returning.

6.21 — Colonel Park Chin-kyŏng's successor: Lieutenant Colonel Ch'oe Kyŏng-rok became 11th Regiment Commander, and Major Song Yo-ch'an became deputy commander.

6.30 — Military operations were suspended due to heavy rainfall.

7.1 — Cheju Police Chief Kim Bong-ho, promising to eliminate illegal corruption in the police, declared that those who surrendered would be recognized as loyal citizens. The travel pass system was abolished and the fishing ban was lifted.

7.5 — The travel pass system between Mokpo and Cheju was abolished.

7.10 — 100 railway police were dispatched to Cheju Island.

7.15 — The 9th Regiment was separated from the 11th Regiment and reorganized (Commander Major Song Yo-ch'an, Deputy Commander Captain Sŏ Chong-ch'ŏl).

7.19 — 200 railway police were dispatched to Cheju Island.

7.20 — Syngman Rhee was elected the first President of the Republic of Korea by the National Assembly.

7.21 — Two companies of the 3rd Brigade moved from Busan to Cheju Island and were attached to the 9th Regiment.

7.22 — The 9th Regiment headquarters moved from the Taech'on barracks in Moseulpo to Cheju town.

**[p. 551]**

**[April 28]** 9th Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryol and armed force commander Kim Dal-sam conduct peace negotiations; agree on cessation of combat within 72 hours

**[April 29]** Military Government Chief Dean visits Jeju Province in secret

Colonel Shue submits report stating "current forces in Jeju Province sufficient to stabilize situation"

Jeju Emergency Martial Defense Commander Kim Jong-ho announces "we are conducting vigorous operations prohibiting passage after 8 PM throughout the province and executing violators"

**[May 1]** So-called "Orari Arson Incident" occurs; peace negotiations break down

Armed forces assassinate election management committee chairman in Dopyong-ri, Jeju town

**[May 3]** US military leadership orders Defense Force headquarters to "launch full-scale attack on armed forces and resolve Jeju incident quickly"

New York Times reports armed forces in Jeju Province presented five surrender conditions: confiscation of police weapons, punishment of police and Western Youth Corps, cancellation of May 10 elections guarantee, and others

**[May 5]** "May 5 Supreme Leadership Conference" held in Jeju Town US Military Government reception room with Military Government Chief Dean, Civil Government Minister An Jae-hong, Police Chief Cho Byong-ok, Defense Force Commander Song Ho-sung, Colonel Mansfield, Governor You Hae-jin, 9th Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryol, Police Surveillance Office Chief Choi Cheon, and others

Armed forces assassinate election management committee chairman in Hwabuk-ri and village chief in Naedo-ri

**[May 6]** US Military Government dismisses 9th Regiment Commander Kim Ik-ryol; Colonel Park Chin-kyong appointed new 9th Regiment Commander

**[May 10]** May 10 elections held. Jeju Province records lowest voting rate at 62.8%. Two election districts (North Jeju-gun A and B) invalidated due to less than majority turnout

Armed forces raid Section 2 of Sangye-ri, Jungmun-myeon; kidnap and assassinate Great Oriental Corps Commander and his wife and National Association representative for Sangye-ri

**[May 11]** Armed forces successively kidnap and assassinate Jeju town Dodu-ri village election management committee chairman, Great Oriental Youth Corps commander, or their family members through May 19

**[May 12]** US Military Government urgently dispatches destroyer USS Craig for coastal blockade of Jeju Province

**[May 15]** 11th Regiment moves from Suwon to Jeju (Colonel Park Chin-kyong, former 9th Regiment Commander, assumes command); existing 9th Regiment incorporated into 11th Regiment

**[May 18]** National Assembly Elections Committee recommends to Military Government Chief Dean that elections be invalidated for North Jeju-gun A and B districts

Metropolitan Police Deputy Chief Kim Nan-su leads special investigation unit dispatched to Jeju Province

**[May 19]** 350 railroad police and 100 police from 6th and 8th command areas, total 450, dispatch from Jeju under Police Ministry order

**[May 20]** US Military Government appoints Colonel Brown, commander of 20th Regiment stationed in Gwangju under US 6th Division, as Jeju Area US Military Commander

**[p. 552]**

41 defense corps members desert from Mosulpo base

**[May 21]** US Military Government announces Oh Yong-guk elected National Assembly representative from South Jeju-gun

**[May 22]** 20 of 41 deserting defense corps members arrested near Daejong

**[May 25]** South Korean Labor Party organ "Labor and People" makes first report on Jeju Province situation

**[May 26]** Military Government Chief Dean announces elections invalidated for North Jeju-gun A and B districts; declares re-elections will be held June 23

**[May 28]** Governor You Hae-jin removed; Im Kwan-ho, Jeju Province native, appointed new governor

Police Chief Cho Byong-ok visits Jeju Province for security situation inspection

**[May 31]** Constitutional National Assembly opens. Syngman Rhee elected National Assembly Speaker

**[Late May]** Adviser Roberts, General Staff adviser, inspects Jeju Province

**[June 1]** 11th Regiment Commander Park Chin-kyong promoted to Colonel

**[June 2]** Jeju-stationed US Military Commander Colonel Brown states "we are conducting operations sweeping completely from west to east of Jeju Province"

**[June 10]** Military Government Chief Dean announces Administrative Order No. 22 indefinitely postponing scheduled June 23 re-elections for North Jeju-gun A and B districts

**[June 11]** Jeju Police Surveillance Office Chief Choi Cheon suspended for insufficient supervision and other reasons

**[June 17]** Kim Bong-ho, Jeju Province native, appointed Jeju Police Surveillance Office Chief

**[June 18]** 11th Regiment Commander Park Chin-kyong assassinated at quarters by subordinate. Military Government Chief Dean and Adviser Roberts descend to Jeju for on-site investigation, recover Park's body, and depart

**[June 21]** Colonel Choi Kyong-rok assumes office as new 11th Regiment Commander; Major Song Yo-chan appointed deputy commander, succeeding Colonel Park Chin-kyong

**[June 30]** Heavy rain halts Defense Force operations

**[July 1]** Jeju Police Surveillance Office Chief Kim Bong-ho announces promise to eliminate police illegal wrongdoing and recognition of surrendering persons as common citizens

Travel permit system for province abolished; fishing ban lifted

**[July 5]** Travel permit system between Mokpo-Jeju abolished on regular liaison ship

**[July 10]** 100 railroad police dispatched to Jeju Province

**[July 15]** 9th Regiment released from 11th Regiment and reorganized (Major Song Yo-chan as Regiment Commander, Captain So Jong-chol as Deputy Commander)

**[July 19]** 200 railroad police dispatched to Jeju Province

**[July 20]** Syngman Rhee elected as inaugural President of Republic of Korea in National Assembly

**[July 21]** Two battalions of 3rd Brigade move from Busan to Jeju Province and assigned to 9th Regiment

**[July 22]** 9th Regiment headquarters moves from Chocheon-myeon Daechon barracks to Jeju town for operational reasons

**[p. 553]**

7.24 — The 11th Regiment moved from Cheju Island to Suwŏn in Kyŏnggi Province.

8.5 — The 9th Regiment's U.S. military advisor reported that people of Cheju origin had been excluded from the intelligence division (S-2).

8.6 — The First Police District Command dispatched a second contingent of reinforcements to replace the first group.

8.11 — The Cheju Island Civil Guard was established.

8.12 — The 9th Regiment's U.S. military advisor reported that people of Cheju origin had been excluded from the operations division (S-3).

8.13 — The Cheju Island travel pass system was reinstated.

8.14 — A military court martial regarding Colonel Park's assassination. Moon Sang-kil, Shin Sang-u, Son Sŏn-ho, and Pae Kyŏng-yong were sentenced to execution; Yang Hoe-ch'ŏn was sentenced to life imprisonment; Kang Sŭng-kyu was sentenced to five years imprisonment.

8.15 — The Republic of Korea government was officially proclaimed.

8.20 — Around August 20, reinforcement police numbering about 800 were sent to Cheju.

8.21 — Kim Dal-sam was elected as a member of the Presidium at the South Korean People's Representatives Conference held in Haiju.

8.24 — President Syngman Rhee and U.S. Military Commander in Korea John R. Hodge signed the "Korea-U.S. Military Security Interim Agreement," whereby operational control of the Korean military continued to remain with the U.S. military.

8.25 — The Cheju Island Emergency Security Command issued a proclamation containing a warning of "the most intense suppression campaign yet to come." One squad of the U.S. 1st Infantry Regiment arrived to replace the military force stationed in Cheju.

8.26 — The U.S. Temporary Military Advisory Group (PMAG) was established.

8.27 — U.S. Military Commander in Korea General Hodge was replaced, and General Coltart was appointed as the new U.S. Military Commander in Korea.

8.29 — The 800-person reinforcement police arrived on Cheju Island.

8.31 — The 7th Police District Command of South Kyŏngsan Province dispatched reinforcements to Cheju Island.

9.8 — A thirteen-year-old boy residing at Samyang-ri, Cheju town, died from torture at Samyang Substation.

9.9 — The Democratic People's Republic of Korea was proclaimed with Kim Il-sŏng as premier and Pak Hŏn-yŏng, Hong Myŏng-hui, and Kim Chaek as vice-premiers.

9.19 — The Soviet Union announced its plan to withdraw troops stationed in North Korea by the end of the year, in accordance with UN resolutions.

9.23 — Moon Sang-kil and Son Sŏn-ho were executed; Shin Sang-u and Pae Kyŏng-yong received special pardons shortly before execution and had their sentences reduced.

9.27 — A general amnesty decree (Presidential Decree No. 6) was proclaimed.

10.1 — Chief of Staff Chŏng Il-gwŏn and Chief of Staff of the Coastal Guard Kim Yŏng-ch'ŏl inspected Cheju.

10.2 — Reinforcement police from the Seoul Police Department and the 8th Police District were dispatched to Cheju Island.

10.5 — Kim Bong-ho from Cheju was appointed Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau Chief, replacing the previous chief from South P'yŏng Province, Hong Sun-bong.

10.8 — Syngman Rhee requested the postponement of the U.S. military withdrawal.

10.9 — General Roberts, the military advisor group chief, urged Captain Treadwell, the military advisor to the 5th Brigade, to become involved more effectively in Cheju operations.

10.11 — The Cheju Island Military Security Command (Commander Colonel Kim Sang-gyŏm) was established.

10.17 — 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an issued a proclamation imposing a travel ban on areas more than 5 kilometers from the Cheju coast, with orders to shoot violators regardless of circumstances.

10.18 — The Cheju coastal blockade was implemented. An order to reinforce Cheju Island was issued to the 14th Regiment stationed in Yŏsu.

10.19 — The 14th Regiment rebellion broke out in Yŏsu. Cheju Island Military Security Commander Colonel Kim Sang-gyŏm was dismissed due to being held accountable for the 14th Regiment rebellion. 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an concurrently served as Cheju Island Military Security Commander.

10.23 — Armed guerrillas launched simultaneous attacks on Samyang Substation in Cheju town and Chojŏn and Hamdŏk substations in Chojŏn-myŏn.

10.24 — Armed guerrillas issued a declaration of war in the name of Yi Tŏk-ku, making a proclamation to suppression forces.

10.28 — About 100 personnel of the 9th Regiment were taken into custody on suspicion of being South Korean Labor Party provocateurs in contact with the armed guerrillas. A U.S. military report stated: "Through covert recruitment, Northwest Youth Association members were dispatched to Cheju." The suppression forces conducted a large-scale mopping-up operation in the Aewŏl-myŏn area and reported complete encirclement and elimination of about 100 members of the Aewŏl and Taejŏng branches near Kosung-ri.

Late October — Chief of Staff Chae Byŏng-dŏk of the Liaison Bureau inspected Cheju.

11.1 — A so-called "police provocateur incident" occurred in which some police were arrested on suspicion of contact with the armed guerrillas.

11.7 — The suppression forces set fire to some 20 houses and shot about 10 residents in Haengwŏn-ri, Kujwa-myŏn. Military and police joint suppression forces raided inland villages at Ŭigwi-ri, Sumang-ri, and Hannam-ri in Namwŏn-myŏn, shooting elderly people and children who had not fled and setting most houses on fire. Armed guerrillas raided Sŏgwi-ri in Sŏgwi-myŏn and set fire to civilian homes.

11.8 — General Roberts, commander of the U.S. military advisory group, reported to the U.S. military commander: "The CIA is performing admirably, and 9th Regiment Commander Major Song Yo-ch'an is engaged in strong and positive activities."

11.9 — Cheju Island General Affairs Bureau Director Kim Tu-hyŏn died from torture at the Northwest Youth Association office.

11.13 — The suppression forces set fire to houses and mass-executed 25 people of all ages in Haga-ri, Aewŏl-myŏn, then mass-executed 50 to 60 residents at Sogil-ri Wŏndong village. Beginning from this day, for approximately four months, inland villages were devastated and residents were mass-executed.

11.15 — General Roberts reported to the U.S. military commander the excellent performance of the CIA and informed him of the plan to "primarily fill the 3 Korean military companies dispatched to Cheju Island with Northwest Youth Association members."

11.17 — President Syngman Rhee proclaimed martial law throughout Cheju Island by Presidential Decree No. 31.

11.19 — The Cheju Police Surveillance Bureau was reorganized into the Cheju Police Bureau.

11.20 — The Ministry of Defense, under the pretext of protecting military operations and military secrets and achieving accuracy in reporting, announced prior censorship of military and official news articles.

11.27 — General Coltart stated: "The advisors under General Roberts, the military advisor group chief, are making satisfactory progress. They are stationed in all Korean military field units."

11.28 — Armed guerrillas conducted intensive attacks on Namwŏn-ri and Wimi-ri in Namwŏn-myŏn, mass-killing residents and setting fire to houses.

11.30 — Law No. 9, the National Defense Organization Act, was proclaimed. The National Security Act was proclaimed. General Roberts sent a letter to the Ministry of Defense explaining how martial law should be implemented.

12.1 — The first martial law military court martial was opened. Records show that sentences were handed down against 871 civilians from December 3 through December 27 over a total of 12 sessions. Armed guerrillas conducted a large-scale attack on Sehwa-ri, Kujwa-myŏn, the site of a police substation, killed about 50 residents, and set fire to 150 buildings in 40 houses. 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an reported to the U.S. Temporary Military Advisory Group: "Between November 20 and 27, 122 rebels were captured alive and 576 were killed."

12.6 — 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an submitted a letter of recommendation to the U.S. 24th Army commander, stating: "U.S. pilot Lieutenant Erickson has provided excellent support in suppressing the rebellion through reconnaissance flights from October 10 to the present."

12.12 — The UN General Assembly approved the Republic of Korea government and called for the prompt withdrawal of U.S. and Soviet troops.

12.13 — 620 members of the Northwest Youth Association were appointed as regular police officers.

12.15 — Pursuant to the National Defense Organization Act, the Liaison Bureau was renamed the Ministry of Defense and the Chosun Defense Force was renamed the Republic of Korea Army. The 9th Regiment was separated from the 5th Brigade and incorporated into the 2nd Brigade. The suppression forces assembled Tossan-ri residents of Pyŏsŏn-myŏn and took some 150 people, including males aged 18 to 40 and some young women, to Pyŏsŏn National School, where they were confined and then mass-executed on December 18 and 19.

12.16 — The advance unit of the 2nd Regiment arrived on Cheju Island.

12.17 — The U.S. State Department requested reconsideration of "NSC-8," the U.S. Korea Policy Guideline that decided to withdraw U.S. forces from Korea by the end of December 1948. A U.S. military report stated: "Recent suppression operations by the 9th Regiment have continued to be successful, and the reason is the desire to implement high-level operations and the desire to live up to the excellent achievements of the 2nd Regiment successors."

12.18 — General Roberts sent letters to Prime Minister Yi Pŏm-sŏk and Chief of Staff Chae Byŏng-dŏk, repeatedly praising 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-ch'an's leadership ability and recommending that these facts be widely publicized through newspapers, broadcasts, and presidential statements. The suppression forces discovered a so-called "daraksiguil" cave where women and children from Hado-ri and Chongdal-ri in Kujwa-myŏn were hiding, set fire inside the cave, and killed them by asphyxiation.

12.19 — A unit of the 9th Regiment left Cheju and arrived in Taejŏn. The Great Eastern Youth Organization and Northwest Youth Association unified to form the Great Korean Youth Organization. 250 Northwest Youth Association members arrived on Cheju Island. Of these, 25 became police and 225 became soldiers.

12.21 — Chief of Staff Chae Byŏng-dŏk replied to General Roberts' recommendation of December 18, saying: "We will introduce Song Yo-ch'an's activities through statements, recommend the president issue a statement, and award Song Yo-ch'an with a decoration." The suppression forces brought 150 residents from Chojŏn-myŏn who had surrendered at the Hamdŏk-ri battalion headquarters to what was called "Park Sŏng-nae" stream in Cheju town and mass-executed them.
