12.22 — The first battalion of the 2nd Regiment departed from Taejŏn and arrived on Cheju Island. The suppression forces mass-executed 76 "fugitive family members" from among the relocated residents at Kashi-ri, Pyŏsŏn-myŏn at a location above what was called "Beodeulmŏt."

12.25 — The Soviet Union announced the complete withdrawal of Soviet troops stationed in North Korea.

12.29 — The 2nd Regiment (Commander Ham Byŏng-sŏn) replaced the 9th Regiment and was stationed in Cheju.

12.30 — A Ministry of Defense spokesperson announced at a press conference: "Since we have concluded the mopping-up of rebels, martial law will be lifted within a few days."

12.31 — Martial law in the Cheju Island District was lifted.

1949

1.1 — Armed guerrillas attacked the 2nd Regiment's 3rd Battalion headquarters located at Odŭng-ri, Cheju town. Following the firefight, about 10 armed guerrillas were killed and 7 soldiers of the 2nd Regiment were killed in action.

1.3 — Armed guerrillas made surprise attacks on Samyang-ri in Cheju town, Harye-ri in Namwŏn-myŏn, and Hyŏpchae-ri in Hallim-myŏn, killing residents. Outdo Substation police and special commando members, disguised as armed guerrillas, entered Dopae-ri, Cheju town, and shot about 70 people over the following day despite their resistance.

1.4 — 2nd Regiment Commander Ham Byŏng-sŏn requested the continuous implementation of martial law. The suppression forces mass-executed residents of Konŭl-tong, Hwabok-ri, Cheju town, over two days.

1.7 — The 2nd Regiment headquarters moved to the Agricultural School.

1.12 — Armed guerrillas attacked the 2nd Regiment's 2nd Company stationed in Ŭigwi-ri, Namwŏn-myŏn, but were repulsed. Following the battle, soldiers mass-executed about 80 residents of inland villages who had been housed at Ŭigwi National School.

1.13 — Armed guerrillas attacked Sŏng'ŭp-ri, killing 38 residents and setting fire to houses.

**[p. 554]**

**[October 11]** Jeju Area Defense Command (Commander Colonel Kim Sang-gyom) established

**[October 17]** 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-chan announces proclamation imposing prohibition on movement beyond 5 km from Jeju coast, declaring execution by shooting for violations regardless of reason

**[October 18]** Jeju coastal blockade

14th Regiment, one battalion from Yosu-stationed unit, reinforced to Jeju Province

**[October 19]** 14th Regiment rebellion incident in Yosu occurs

Jeju Area Defense Commander Colonel Kim Sang-gyom removed for responsibility in 14th Regiment rebellion; 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-chan assumes concurrent position

**[October 23]** Armed forces simultaneously attack Samyang Police Substation in Jeju town and Chocheon and Hamdok Police Substations in Chocheon-myeon

**[October 24]** Armed forces issue declaration of war to government under name of Lee Tok-gu; issue appeal to suppression forces

**[October 28]** About 100 9th Regiment soldiers arrested on suspicion of being South Korean Labor Party agents in contact with armed forces

US military report: "infiltrators dispatched Northwestern Youth Corps members to Jeju through covert recruitment"

Suppression forces report complete encirclement and annihilation of about 100 Aewol and Daejong branch members near Gosong-ri following large-scale suppression operations in Aewol-myeon area

**[Late October]** Chairman of Military Advisory Council General Staff Chae Byong-dok inspects Jeju Province

**[November 1]** So-called "police agents incident" occurs: some police arrested for suspicion of contact with armed forces

**[November 7]** Suppression forces set fire to 20 houses in Haeongwon-ri, Gujwa-myeon and shoot more than 10 residents

Joint military-police suppression forces raid mountain villages of Ui-gwi-ri, Su-mang-ri, and Han-nam-ri in Namwon-myeon; shoot elderly and children who did not evacuate; set fire to most buildings

Armed forces raid Sogwi-ri, Sogwi-myeon and set fire to private residences

**[November 8]** US Military Advisory Group Chief Roberts reports to US military commander "CIA is performing excellently; 9th Regiment Commander Lieutenant Colonel Song Yo-chan conducting powerful and vigorous activities"

**[November 9]** Jeju Province General Affairs Bureau Director Kim Doo-hyun dies after torture at Northwestern Youth Corps office

**[November 13]** Suppression forces set fire to houses in Haga-ri, Aewol-myeon and execute 25 men, women, and children by mass shooting; subsequently execute 50-60 residents by mass shooting in Sogil-ri Wendong village; beginning from this date, level mountain villages to waste and conduct mass executions of residents for approximately four months

**[November 15]** Roberts, chief of advisory group, praises CIA activities and reports to US military commander "plan to fill three Korean military battalions dispatched to Jeju Province primarily with Northwestern Youth Corps members"

**[November 17]** President Syngman Rhee proclaims martial law throughout Jeju Province by Presidential Order No. 31

**[November 19]** Jeju Police Surveillance Office reorganized into Jeju Provincial Police

**[November 20]** Ministry of Defense announces military censorship of all military-related news articles under pretext of protecting military operations and secrets and ensuring accuracy of reporting

**[p. 555]**

**[November 27]** General Coltier states "Satisfactory progress achieved by advisory group members under military adviser Roberts. They are deployed in all Korean military field units"

**[November 28]** Armed forces concentrate attacks on Namwon-ri and Wimi-ri in Namwon-myeon; mass murder of residents and arson

**[November 30]** National Defense Organization Law (No. 9) promulgated

**[December 1]** National Security Law promulgated

Roberts, chief of advisory group, sends letter to Ministry of Defense explaining implementation of martial law

**[December 3]** First Martial Law Court-Martial revised. Records show civilian verdicts delivered over 12 sessions from December 3-27; 871 civilians found guilty

Armed forces conduct concentrated attack on Sehwa-ri, Gujwa-myeon, police substation location; murder about 50 residents and set 150 structures in 40 households ablaze

9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-chan reports to US temporary military advisory group "122 rebels captured and 576 executed between November 20-27"

**[December 6]** 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-chan sends letter of recommendation to US 24th Army commander praising US pilot Lieutenant Erikson's excellent support for suppressing insurrection through reconnaissance flights from October 10 to present

**[December 12]** UN General Assembly approves Republic of Korea government while demanding prompt withdrawal of US and Soviet forces

**[December 13]** 620 Northwestern Youth Corps members appointed as regular police

**[December 15]** Under National Defense Organization Law, Military Advisory Council becomes Ministry of Defense; Chosun Defense Force renamed Republic of Korea Army

9th Regiment released from 2nd Brigade and incorporated into 2nd Brigade

Suppression forces assemble Tosari-ri residents in Pyosun-myeon; transport 150 youths ages 18-40 and some young women to Pyosun Elementary School and confine; execute by mass shooting on December 18-19

**[December 16]** 2nd Regiment advance party arrives in Jeju

**[December 17]** US State Department requests reconsideration of NSC-8 US Korea policy directive determining withdrawal of US forces from Korea by end of December 1948

US military report: "recent 9th Regiment suppression operations continue to succeed; reason is desire to conduct skilled operations and desire to match accomplishments of excellent 2nd Regiment personnel"

**[December 18]** Roberts, chief of advisory group, sends letters to Prime Minister Lee Bom-suck and General Staff Chairman Chae Byong-dok repeatedly praising 9th Regiment Commander Song Yo-chan's command abilities; recommends widespread publicity through newspapers, radio, and presidential statements

Suppression forces discover "Drang Shu Cave" where residents from Hado-ri and Jongdal-ri, Gujwa-myeon including 3 women and children are hiding; set fire inside cave causing suffocation deaths

**[p. 556]**

**[December 19]** 9th Regiment advance party departs Jeju, arrives in Daejeon

Great Oriental Youth Corps and Northwestern Youth Corps unified and Great Korean Youth Corps established

250 Northwestern Youth Corps members arrive in Jeju; 25 become police; 225 become soldiers

**[December 21]** General Staff Chairman Chae Byong-dok replies to Roberts' December 18 recommendation "will introduce Song Yo-chan's activities through statements; recommend president issue statement; will award Song Yo-chan decoration"

Suppression forces take 150 residents from Chocheon-myeon who surrendered at Hamdok-ri battalion headquarters to streambed called "Baksung-nae" in Jeju town and execute by mass shooting

**[December 22]** 1st Battalion of 2nd Regiment departing Daejeon arrives in Jeju

Suppression forces execute 76 "families of persons evading" selected from residents in Gasi-ri, Pyosun-myeon by mass shooting in field above "Beodeul Pond"

**[December 25]** Soviet Union announces complete withdrawal of Soviet forces stationed in North Korea

**[December 29]** 2nd Regiment (Commander Colonel Ham Byong-sun) remains stationed in Jeju, replacing 9th Regiment

**[December 30]** Ministry of Defense Spokesman announces at press conference "suppression of rebels considered complete; martial law will be lifted within several days"

**[December 31]** Jeju Area martial law lifted

**1949**

**[January 1]** Armed forces attack 2nd Regiment 3rd Battalion base in Odung-ri, Jeju town. Following combat, about 10 armed force members killed; 7 soldiers from 2nd Regiment killed in action

**[January 3]** Armed forces raid Samyang-ri in Jeju town, Harye-ri in Namwon-myeon, Hyeopjae-ri in Hallim-myeon; kill residents

Oedo Police Substation police and special corps members disguised as armed forces enter Dopyong-ri, Jeju town; shoot about 70 residents despite some population resistance; killing continues through next day

**[January 4]** 2nd Regiment Commander Ham Byong-sun demands continuation of martial law

Suppression forces execute village residents from Hwabuk-ri, Gongeul-dong section by mass shooting over two days

**[January 7]** 2nd Regiment headquarters moves to Agricultural School

**[January 12]** Armed forces raid 2nd Regiment 2nd Company stationed in Ui-gwi-ri, Namwon-myeon but are repulsed. Immediately following combat, military personnel execute about 80 residents from mountain villages confined in Ui-gwi Elementary School by mass shooting

**[January 13]** Armed forces raid Sungup-ri, massacre 38 residents, and commit arson

**[p. 557]**

## 2. Jeju 4·3 Incident Chronology

1.17
- "Bukchon Incident" occurs. In retaliation for soldiers being ambushed near the village, suppression forces burn all of Bukchon-ri in Chochan-myŏn and conduct mass executions of approximately 400 residents over the next day.

1.18
- Third District Police Station (Mosulp'o) and Fourth District Police Station (Sŏngsan-p'o) established.

1.20
- 2nd Regiment transferred from existing 2nd Brigade affiliation to direct control of the Army Headquarters.

1.21
- President Syngman Rhee mentions the incidents in Cheju and Chŏlla regions at a state council meeting, stating: "Although the United States recognizes Korea's importance and expresses much sympathy, the underlying causes of the Cheju Island and Chŏlla incidents must be completely eradicated (拔根塞源) so that their aid will become more active, and it is necessary to suppress gangsters engaged in looting and theft in local areas using severe methods to demonstrate the dignity of the law," issuing this directive.

1.22
- Army Headquarters orders the Army Aviation Command to dispatch two aircraft to Cheju Island by January 24th to cooperate with suppression operations.
- Suppression forces conduct mass executions of approximately 80 residents from Tonggwang-ri and Sangch'ang-ri in Andeok-myŏn near Chŏngbang Waterfall in Sŏguipo.

1.24
- State Council decides to dispatch one battalion of ROK Army to Cheju Island.

1.25
- Two L-5 aircraft of the Korean military are dispatched to Cheju Island.

1.28
- President Syngman Rhee states at a state council meeting: "The U.S. Navy has called at Cheju Island with good results, and one battalion of military forces and 1,000 police personnel have been dispatched, so complete the pacification (完征) speedily," issuing this directive.

1.31
- Army Headquarters dispatches a guerrilla battalion under the 6th Brigade, a specialized unit for guerrilla warfare, to Cheju.

2.4
- Armed guerrillas ambush 2nd Regiment forces heading to Cheju City to return Type 99 rifles to their regiment near Kimnyŏng-ri in Kuja-myŏn, seize 150 rifles, and kill 15 soldiers of the 2nd Regiment and one policeman.
- Joint operations of the Army, Navy, and Air Force are launched against the Ponggae district (Ponggae, Yonggane, and Hoechon villages) in Cheju City. Suppression forces pursue fleeing residents and execute hundreds.

2.5
- Public Information Director Kim Dong-sŏng announces: "The state of emergency in Cheju Island that went into effect on November 17, 1948 was lifted a month ago, but there has been no official announcement regarding its effect." In response, U.S. forces comment: "Both Koreans and Americans have often referred to the state of emergency as martial law. However, this is clearly incorrect. Martial law has never been proclaimed by the Korean government."

2.12
- Kwanŭm-sa Temple is burned by 2nd Regiment soldiers. (In addition, 15 other temples in the province were completely burned by suppression forces, 3 were partially burned, and 9 temple inmates were released during the evacuation order. Additionally, 16 Buddhist monks were killed by suppression forces. Meanwhile, one temple in Hamdŏk-ri whose chief priest was a police officer suffered damage from armed guerrillas.)

2.19
- 505 members of the Police Special Unit (Commander Police Major Kim Tae-il) are dispatched to Cheju.

2.20
- U.S. Military Advisory Group reports: "Near Todu-ri in Cheju City, militia members under the supervision of military and police stabbed 76 people to death with spears."

2.23
- Prosecutor General issues a directive not to treat violators of the National Security Law leniently and to take strong measures.

**[p. 558]**

2.26
- Police stations renamed (1st District Police Station → Cheju Police Station; 2nd District Police Station → Sŏguipo Police Station; 3rd District Police Station → Mosulp'o Police Station; 4th District Police Station → Sŏngsan-p'o Police Station).

2.27
- 2nd Regiment carries out executions of 39 individuals sentenced to death by court-martial in December 1948 at Hwabuk-ri in Cheju City.

3.2
- Jeju Combat Command Headquarters (Commander Colonel Yu Chae-hŭng; Chief of Staff 2nd Regiment Commander Ham Pyŏng-sŏn) established.

3.10
- Prime Minister Yi Pŏm-sŏk and Interior Minister Sin Sŏng-mo inspect Cheju Island.

3.14
- General Roberts notifies the U.S. Mission in a document that three U.S. military aircraft were mobilized for operations in Cheju Island.

3.21
- Announcement that re-election for Cheju Island will be held on May 10, 1949.
- Prime Minister Yi Pŏm-sŏk relinquishes concurrent appointment as Defense Minister; Sin Sŏng-mo is appointed as Defense Minister.

3.23
- U.S. President approves "NSC-8/2," the Korean policy directive delaying the withdrawal of U.S. forces from Korea until the end of June 1949.

4.1
- U.S. military report states: "The 9th Regiment adopted a program of mass slaughter of residents in mid-mountain villages to eradicate all resistance, and as of March 1949 there were 15,000 casualties on Cheju Island, and while there are rumors that guerrillas receive logistical support from the mainland or North Korea, there is no evidence whatsoever to substantiate such reports," submitting a comprehensive report of the situation to date.

4.5
- Marine Corps established.

4.7
- By special order of President Syngman Rhee, Defense Minister Sin Sŏng-mo and Social Affairs Minister Yi Yun-yŏng visit Cheju Island.

4.9
- President Syngman Rhee visits Cheju Island with his wife.
- Registration of voters and candidates for Cheju Island re-election closes.

4.14
- Defense Minister Sin Sŏng-mo returns to Seoul after inspecting Cheju Island.

4.16
- Defense Minister Sin Sŏng-mo and U.S. Military Advisory Group Commander Roberts meet and agree to withdraw members of the Northwest Youth Association from Cheju Island.

5.10
- National Assembly member re-election held. Hong Sun-nyŏng and Yang Byŏng-jik elected.

5.15
- Jeju Combat Command Headquarters dissolved. 3rd Battalion of 2nd Regiment, composed of Northwest Youth Association members, withdraws.

5.18
- Emergency Security Commander Kim Tae-il and police special unit withdraw to Seoul.

5.25
- Guerrilla battalion is relieved of assignment from 2nd Regiment and withdraws.

6.1
- 2nd Regiment Commander Ham Pyŏng-sŏn promoted to colonel.

6.5
- National Guidance League proclamation rally held.

6.7
- Armed Guerrilla Commander-in-Chief Yi Tŏk-ku killed by police.

6.20
- 2nd Regiment incorporated from direct Army Headquarters control into Seoul Security Command.

6.23
- High Court-Martial held. Military court proceedings held 10 times from June 23rd to July 7th, with guilty verdicts rendered for 1,659 civilians on charges of "providing aid and communication to the enemy and espionage," according to the record.

**[p. 559]**

6.29
- Withdrawal of U.S. forces completed. 500 U.S. military advisors remain.

7.7
- 2nd Regiment 2nd Battalion withdraws to Inch'ŏn (only 1st Battalion remains).

7.15
- Independent 1st Battalion (Commander Kim Yong-ju) moves from Suwon to Cheju Island.

8.13
- 2nd Regiment transfers complete responsibility for security of Cheju area to Independent 1st Battalion and fully withdraws.

8.20
- Jeju Security Command Headquarters established (commanding officer of Cheju-stationed units becomes security commander).

8.26
- Homeland Defense Army redesignated as Reserve Force.

8.27
- Vice Interior Minister Chang Kyŏng-gŭn inspects Cheju Island.

9.14
- Mokp'o Penitentiary breakout occurs. 286 escapees are executed.

10.2
- 249 individuals sentenced to death in the "1949 court-martial" executed by firing squad near Cheju airfield and secretly buried.

11.15
- Kim Ch'ung-hŭi, Cheju branch chief of the National Society, appointed governor of Cheju Island.

11.24
- Martial Law Act promulgated.

11.27
- Security Bureau announces that as of November 27th, the number of converts who joined the National Guidance League in Cheju has reached 5,283.

12.20
- Cheju Island Reconstruction and Development Committee (Chairman Governor Kim Ch'ung-hŭi) organized.

12.27
- Independent 1st Battalion withdraws from Cheju.

12.28
- Marine Corps (Commander Colonel Sin Hyŏn-jun) arrives in Cheju.

**[p. 560]**

1950

2.10
- Governor Kim Ch'ung-hŭi reports through an official document to the Prime Minister that the 4·3 Incident caused approximately 30,000 casualties and property losses of approximately 40,000 houses, totaling approximately 2 billion wŏn in damages.

5.30
- Second National Assembly elections held. In Cheju Island, Kim In-sŏn, Kang Ch'ang-yong, and Kang Kyŏng-ok elected.

6.25
- Korean War breaks out. Cheju Island Marine Commander also serves as Cheju Security Commander.
- Security Bureau Director urgently issues a directive to police bureaus throughout the country by telephone regarding "nationwide suspect roundup and nationwide penitentiary security" and orders immediate arrest of all nationwide suspects.

6.29
- Security Bureau Director issues directive to Cheju Island Police Director regarding "arrest of subversive elements," commanding: "Arrest members of the National Guidance League and other subversive elements; they must not be released until orders from this bureau are issued."

7.6
- "Submission of list of all Cheju Area preliminary detainees" directive issued from Cheju Security Commander to Cheju Police Director.

**[p. 561]**

7.8
- Martial law proclaimed throughout South Korea except Chŏlla provinces pursuant to Article 1 of the Martial Law Act.

7.11
- Security Bureau Director issues "arrest of subversive elements" directive to Cheju Police Director.

7.15
- One battalion of Marine Corps departs Cheju Port and moves to Kunsan Port.

7.16
- Army 5th Training Center established in Cheju Island.

7.20
- Emergency martial law expanded to entire South Korea.

7.25
- Armed guerrillas attack Hawŏn-ri in Chungmun-myŏn and commit arson on civilian homes.

7.27
- Suppression forces drown people previously detained at Cheju City Main Liquor Factory through preliminary detention at sea before Sŏra Peak.

7.29
- Approximately 150 detainees previously detained in Sŏguipo Police Station jurisdiction are dragged out and drowned at sea.

8.4
- Presidential Emergency Order No. 9 promulgates Emergency Homeland Defense Ordinance.
- Police official document ("arrest of subversive elements") clarifies that 820 people are in preliminary detention in Cheju Province as of August 4th.
- Several hundred preliminary detainees detained at Cheju Police Station, main liquor factory, and other locations are drowned in the sea before Cheju Port.

8.5
- Marine Corps recruit entrance ceremony held at Mosulp'o unit.
- 423 student volunteers from Ohyŏn Middle School enlist as student soldiers.

8.8
- Sixteen prominent local figures including Cheju District Prosecutor and judges are arrested and detained on suspicion of forming a "Committee for Welcoming the People's Army."

8.19
- From the night of the 19th through dawn of the 20th, several hundred preliminary detainees held in Cheju Police Station detention are executed by firing squad at Cheju Airfield and secretly buried.

8.20
- Of 344 preliminary detainees in Hanrim-myŏn, Taejŏng-myŏn, and Andeok-myŏn under Mosulp'o Police Station jurisdiction, 252 are transferred to the military and executed by mass firing squad on Sŏtal Peak (Seot-al-oreum). Due to official restrictions, remains were not recovered until six years later. Unable to identify the remains of victims from Taejŏng-myŏn, bereaved families appropriately matched bones and created 132 burial mounds, calling them "Monument of a Hundred Ancestors and One Grandson" (百祖一孫之墓).

8.30
- Marine Corps Intelligence Officer Kim Tu-ch'an issues official document to Sŏngsan-p'o Police Station Commander Mun Hyŏng-sun ordering executions of preliminary detainees and requesting a report of execution results, but Commander Mun Hyŏng-sun refuses, stating that it is "improper and unexecuted" (未履行).

8.31
- Some Marine Corps troops withdraw from Cheju Island.

9.3
- "Cheju Island People's Army Welcome Committee Incident" suspects released.

9.14
- Decision made at Cheju Island Buddhist organization representatives' joint meeting to release preliminary detainees deemed to have potential for conversion.

9.15
- Preliminary detainee releases begin.

10.10
- Martial law in Cheju Island lifted.

11.7
- Emergency martial law throughout South Korea lifted. Emergency security martial law proclaimed for all areas south of the 38th parallel except Cheju Island and Kyŏngnam and Kyŏngbuk regions.

**[p. 562]**

1951

1.22
- Army 1st Training Center moves from Taegu to Cheju Island.

4.24
- Cheju Police report military achievements from October 1, 1950 to April 22, 1951 (seven months): armed guerrillas killed 56, weapons seized (rifles 11, hand grenades 2), police casualties 17 (killed 15, wounded 2), self-defense force casualties 24 (killed 11, wounded 11, missing 2), civilian casualties 42 (killed 1, wounded 3, abducted 38).

5.10
- Cheju Island Army Special Investigation Agency established.

5.20
- Number of refugees arriving in Cheju Island tallied at 148,794.

5.28
- Commander-in-Chief of Army, Navy, and Air Force Chŏng Il-gwŏn inspects the Army 1st Training Center in Mosulp'o.

1952

1.7
- Brigadier General Chang Do-yŏng appointed commander of Army Training Center.

1.25
- Korean Youth Association special operation unit holds launching ceremony at Cheju Theater.

2.6
- U.S. 8th Army Commander Van Fleet inspects Cheju Island.

4.1
- Under the guidance of the Security Bureau Operations Guidance Section, Cheju Police conduct "Cheju Island Residual Armed Guerrilla Annihilation Operations" over a planned 30-day period ending April 30th.

5.16
- Army Intelligence Bureau estimates Cheju Island armed guerrilla forces (Commander Kim Sŏng-gyu) at 65 members (30 armed, 35 unarmed).

5.28
- Cheju Island Council passes a resolution releasing a mountain descent advisory to residual armed guerrillas, indicating that life will be guaranteed if they surrender for complete destruction of remaining armed forces.

7.3
- President Syngman Rhee and party, along with U.S. 8th Army Commander Van Fleet and General Yu Chae-hŭng, inspect the Army 1st Training Center in Cheju.

8.9
- Cheju Security Commander and Army 1st Training Center Commander Chang Do-yŏng departs.

8.14
- New Cheju Security Commander and Army 1st Training Center Commander O Dŏk-chun assumes office.

9.16
- Five armed guerrillas intrude into Cheju Broadcasting Station and abduct the broadcast section chief and two others on night duty.

10.31
- Armed guerrillas attack Sŏguipo Power Station and commit arson.

11.1
- Cheju Island Police Headquarters establishes 100 Combat Police Command.

11.26
- President Syngman Rhee instructs at state council meeting: "Do not publicize police preliminary detention."

12.25
- Three police units (one company each) from Kyŏnggi, Ch'ungnam, and Kyŏngbuk provinces dispatched for complete annihilation of residual armed forces in Cheju Island.

**[p. 563]**
